It also replaces `npx prisma` with local binary calls throughout CI and Docker to pin Prisma to the installed version.\n\nKey issues found in new code (on top of issues flagged in previous review rounds):\n\n- **Cost tracker request count is wrong** ÔÇö `requestCount` increments by `1` per flush cycle per project regardless of how many records are batched, causing the cost summary to under-report actual API usage.\n- **Cost tracker race condition** ÔÇö The optimistic read-modify-write in `flushCostBuffer` is not wrapped in a transaction; concurrent flush cycles (periodic timer vs. threshold trigger) can overwrite each other's writes and silently drop cost data.\n- **SSE streaming endpoint uses POST** ÔÇö The `/ai-gateway/stream` endpoint sends SSE headers but is registered as `@Post`, making it incompatible with the browser-native `EventSource` API. There is also no client-disconnect handler, meaning API credits continue to be consumed after the browser navigates away.\n- **`messageLimit` never enforced** ÔÇö The `Project` model adds `messageCount`/`messageLimit` fields to cap AI interactions per project, but `AiGatewayService` never checks this limit before forwarding requests to a provider.\n- **JWT guard logs credential material** ÔÇö The enhanced `JwtAuthGuard` logs a 20-character prefix of the raw `Authorization` header on every auth failure, writing part of the token into log output.\n\n<h3>Confidence Score: 2/5</h3>\n\n- This PR should not merge as-is ÔÇö it contains a credential leak in log output, broken cost accounting, and a quota-enforcement gap that allows unlimited API spend.\n- Several of the new components have correctness issues that will be immediately visible in production: cost data will be silently lost or under-counted on every flush, the message limit is a dead feature, the streaming endpoint cannot be consumed by browser `EventSource`, and every auth failure leaks token bytes into logs. The Prisma schema and idea-capture changes are solid, but the new AI gateway layer needs fixes before shipping.\n- `apps/api/src/modules/ai-gateway/services/cost-tracker.service.ts` (race condition + request count bug), `apps/api/src/modules/ai-gateway/ai-gateway.controller.ts` (POST SSE + disconnect handling), `apps/api/src/modules/ai-gateway/ai-gateway.service.ts` (missing message limit check), and `apps/api/src/modules/auth/guards/jwt-auth.guard.ts` (credential leak in logs).\n\n<h3>Important Files Changed</h3>\n\n\n\n\n| Filename | Overview |\n|----------|----------|\n| apps/api/src/modules/ai-gateway/services/cost-tracker.service.ts | New cost tracking service with two logic bugs: `requestCount` always increments by 1 regardless of batch size, and the non-transactional read-modify-write creates a race condition between concurrent flush cycles that can silently drop cost data. |\n| apps/api/src/modules/ai-gateway/ai-gateway.controller.ts | New AI gateway controller introduces a POST-based SSE streaming endpoint that is incompatible with the browser-native `EventSource` API, and lacks client-disconnect handling which will cause ongoing billable API usage after client disconnects. |\n| apps/api/src/modules/ai-gateway/ai-gateway.service.ts | New AI gateway routing service with provider fallback logic. The `messageLimit` field added to the Project model is never checked here, silently bypassing the intended quota enforcement. |\n| apps/api/src/modules/auth/guards/jwt-auth.guard.ts | JWT guard enhanced with debug logging; logs a 20-character prefix of the raw Authorization header, which leaks credential material into log output. |\n| apps/api/src/modules/ai-gateway/adapters/claude.adapter.ts | New Claude adapter for Anthropic API; correctly handles streaming, token tracking, and cost calculation. **OWASP check constructs a shell command string but passes it to `execFileSync` as the executable name**\n\n   After the allowlist validation, the OWASP command is assembled as a single shell string with additional arguments and shell redirections appended:\n\n   ```ts\n   const fullCommand = `${owaspCommand} --project Quiz2Biz --scan . 2>&1`;\n   const { success } = runCommand(fullCommand, true);\n   ```\n\n   `runCommand` uses `execFileSync`, which does **not** invoke a shell. The entire string `\"/path/to/dependency-check --project Quiz2Biz --scan . 2>&1\"` is treated as a literal executable name ÔÇö Node.js will try to find a binary with that exact name (including spaces), which does not exist. The check will always fail with `ENOENT` regardless of whether the tool is installed or the project is clean.\n\n   The correct form separates the executable from its arguments:\n\n   ```ts\n   const { success } = runCommand(owaspCommand, [\n     '--project', 'Quiz2Biz',\n     '--scan', '.',\n   ], true);\n   ```\n\n   Note this also removes the `2>&1` shell redirection, which `execFileSync` cannot interpret anyway; stderr is already captured via `stdio: 'pipe'` when `silent` is `true`.\n\n   <details><summary>Prompt To Fix With AI</summary>\n\n   `````markdown\n   This is a comment left during a code review.\n   Path: scripts/run-testing-framework.ts\n   Line: 1846-1848\n\n   Comment:\n   **OWASP check constructs a shell command string but passes it to `execFileSync` as the executable name**\n\n   After the allowlist validation, the OWASP command is assembled as a single shell string with additional arguments and shell redirections appended:\n\n   ```ts\n   const fullCommand = `${owaspCommand} --project Quiz2Biz --scan . 2>&1`;\n   const { success } = runCommand(fullCommand, true);\n   ```\n\n   `runCommand` uses `execFileSync`, which does **not** invoke a shell. In production this means the app starts against a potentially stale schema and will fail at runtime with Prisma query errors.\n\n   The original code with `npx prisma` would fail loudly here (npx would attempt to download the binary or exit with an error), which is safer behaviour ÔÇö a failed startup is more recoverable than a successfully-started app silently operating on a wrong schema.\n\n   Consider failing fast instead:\n\n   \n\n   <details><summary>Prompt To Fix With AI</summary>\n\n   `````markdown\n   This is a comment left during a code review.\n   Path: docker/api/entrypoint.sh\n   Line: 15-26\n\n   Comment:\n   **Missing Prisma binary silently skips all database migrations**\n\n   If `./node_modules/.bin/prisma` doesn't exist (e.g., `npm ci` failed, a volume mount problem in Docker, or a layer caching issue), the container prints a single warning line and starts the application with **no migrations applied**. Writing any portion of authorization headers to application logs is a security anti-pattern ÔÇö log aggregation systems such as Datadog or Splunk often have weaker access controls than the application itself, creating an exfiltration surface.\n\n   The `hasAuthHeader` boolean (whether any auth was supplied at all) already conveys the meaningful diagnostic signal. The raw partial value adds no actionable debugging value. Remove `tokenPreview` and the `Token:` portion from the warn statement to avoid logging credential-adjacent data.\n\n   <details><summary>Prompt To Fix With AI</summary>\n\n   `````markdown\n   This is a comment left during a code review.\n   Path: apps/api/src/modules/auth/guards/jwt-auth.guard.ts\n   Line: 744-750\n\n   Comment:\n   **Sensitive header data written to application logs**\n\n   `tokenPreview` captures the first 20 characters of the raw `Authorization` header and writes it to warn-level logs on every auth failure. Writing any portion of authorization headers to application logs is a security anti-pattern ÔÇö log aggregation systems such as Datadog or Splunk often have weaker access controls than the application itself, creating an exfiltration surface.\n\n   The `hasAuthHeader` boolean (whether any auth was supplied at all) already conveys the meaningful diagnostic signal. The raw partial value adds no actionable debugging value. Remove `tokenPreview` and the `Token:` portion from the warn statement to avoid logging credential-adjacent data.\n\n   How can I resolve this? If you propose a fix, please make it concise.\n   `````\n   </details>\n\n6. `prisma/schema.prisma`, line 697-698 ([link](https://github.com/bas-more/quiz2biz/blob/eec90200b3eeb28eb496b9654286aa466d6c7cfa/prisma/schema.prisma#L697-L698)) \n\n   **`fieldValue` and `modelMap` lack `@map` directives ÔÇö inconsistent snake_case convention**\n\n   Two new fields deviate from the established convention of mapping all Prisma camelCase fields to `snake_case` DB column names via `@map`:\n\n   1. `ExtractedFact.fieldValue` ÔÇö generates a column named `fieldValue` (camelCase) in the DB instead of `field_value`.\n   2. `AiProvider.modelMap` ÔÇö generates a column named `modelMap` (camelCase) instead of `model_map`.\n\n   The migration SQL confirms this: `\"fieldValue\" TEXT NOT NULL` and `\"modelMap\" JSONB NOT NULL`. Every other field in these new models (e.g. `confirmed_by_user`, `source_message_id`, `api_endpoint`) correctly uses `@map`.\n\n   Add the missing `@map` directives and update the migration:\n\n   ```prisma\n   // ExtractedFact\n   fieldValue      String   @db.Text @map(\"field_value\")\n\n   // AiProvider\n   modelMap        Json     @default(\"{}\") @map(\"model_map\")\n   ```\n\n   Note: because the migration has already been generated, a new corrective migration will be needed if the database was applied in any environment.\n\n   <details><summary>Prompt To Fix With AI</summary>\n\n   `````markdown\n   This is a comment left during a code review.\n   Path: prisma/schema.prisma\n   Line: 697-698\n\n   Comment:\n   **`fieldValue` and `modelMap` lack `@map` directives ÔÇö inconsistent snake_case convention**\n\n   Two new fields deviate from the established convention of mapping all Prisma camelCase fields to `snake_case` DB column names via `@map`:\n\n   1. `ExtractedFact.fieldValue` ÔÇö generates a column named `fieldValue` (camelCase) in the DB instead of `field_value`.\n   2. `AiProvider.modelMap` ÔÇö generates a column named `modelMap` (camelCase) instead of `model_map`.\n\n   The migration SQL confirms this: `\"fieldValue\" TEXT NOT NULL` and `\"modelMap\" JSONB NOT NULL`.
